1.0 Introduction 
1.1. Background 
ColeEngineering GroupLtd.(ColeEngineering) hasbeenretainedbyTorontoandRegionConservation 
Authority (TRCA)toprovideengineering servicesinsupportofapreliminary assessment oferodingand
failedslopesthroughout BlackCreekwithintheCityofToronto.Theerosionandfailedsitesarearesult
oftheJuly8th2013stormevent.Thesitesarearisktoresidents, guests,andthepublicduetosteep
andunstableslopes.Thisreportwilloutlinetheexistingsiteconditions, discussthedesignalternatives 
investigated, comparepreliminary costestimates andprovideoverallrecommendations forthe
proposed works.
1.2. Site Locations and Existing Conditions 
ThesubjectsitesinAreaEarelocatedthroughout BlackCreekwithintheHumberRiverWatershed in
theCityofToronto.Allofthesitesareprivatelyownedandoccupiedresidential lots.Locationplansfor
eachoftheproperties areprovidedinAppendix A.
Manyofthefailedslopesspreadacrossmultipleproperties andconsistoffailedretainingwallsin
conjunction withsurficialslides.Theerosionattheproperties hascausedthelossofpropertyandposes
arisktotheproperties themselves andadjacentinfrastructure. Sitespecificconditions foreach
propertyarediscussed furtherinthepropertyspecificreportsprovidedafterthisreport.
1.3. Previous Studies 
Togainafullunderstanding ofthesubjectsites,afullreviewofavailablebackground information was
conducted priortoinitiatingtheproject.Previousstudiesthathavebeendeveloped withinthestudy
areawhichassessthesitesareasfollows:
xSlopeStability&ErosionRiskAssessment July8,2013StormDamagePhase2Toronto,
Ontarioprepared forTorontoandRegionConservation Authority, byTerraprobe Inc.,October
16,2013,revisedNovember 6,2013.
Thereportestablished siteconditions forthesitesanddetermined theproperties inAreasEandH
whichrequirefurtherstudypriortorehabilitation. 
2.0 Study Methodology 
Thefollowing stepsarerequiredforthecompletion oftheslopestabilityassessment anddevelopment 
ofthepreliminary designconcepts: 
1. Review background information; 
2. Conduct topographic surveyofsites;
3. Prepare baseplansinAutoCAD; 
4. Visual siteinvestigations toidentifyfactorsthatcouldaffectthestabilityoftheslopes;
5. Geotechnical investigations; 
6. Determine theLongTermStableSlopeCrests(LTSSC);
7. Constraints investigation includingutilitylocatesandconstruction access;
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  Area E
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
WR14-0072 (April 2015)  Page 2 of 2 
8. Develop preliminary designconcepts; 
9. Prepare costestimates forthepreliminary designconcepts; and,
10. Proandconanalysisofthepreliminary designoptions.
3.0 Site Specific Investigations 
TheerosionsitesinAreaEwereindividually investigated andassessedtodevelopsitespecific
recommendations tomitigateerosionrisks.Theinvestigations aresummarized thesectionfollowthis
report.
4.0 Monitoring 
PreͲconstruction andpostͲconstruction erosionmonitoring oftheproposed worksshouldbe
implemented includingarecordofphotographs. Monitoring ofproposed vegetation shouldalsobe
conducted fortwo(2)yearsafterplantingtoensuresurvivability. Themonitoring activitiesshould
include(butnotlimitedto):
xQualitative monitoring oftheperformance andeffectiveness ofinterimmeasures (e.g.nurse
crops)andmonitoring ofplanthealthduringdroughts; 
xQuantitative measurements oferosionifany;
xThegeneralcondition andgeneralperformance oftheproposed erosioncontrol(ESC)
measurewillberecordedonarankedbasis;
xIfmaintenance isrequired, thecontractor shouldbenotifiedimmediately torepairtheESC
measureaccordingly; and,
xPriortotheendofthewarrantyperiodfromthenursery,mortalities shouldbeinventoried 
andreplaced. 
21 PEACHAM CRESCENT 
21 PEACHAM CRESCENT   
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  21 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
1.0 Introduction 
1.1. Location
Thesubjectsiteislocatedattherearof21PeachamCrescentintheCityofToronto,southofthe
intersection ofExburyRoadandPeachamCrescent, westofJaneStreet.Itisnotedtheneighbouring 
propertyat23PeachamCrescentaswellas25PeachamCrescentarealsoincludedinthestudy.21
PeachamCrescentisaprivatelyownedresidential lot.Thesubjectsiteislocatedonthesouthsideof
PeachamCrescentandisboundedby19and23PeachamCrescenttotheeastandwest,ExburyPark
andBlackCreektothesouthandPeachamCrescenttothenorth.
AlocationplanisprovidedasFigureLOCͲPHinAppendix A.
2.0 Existing Conditions 
Thesiteconsistsofanerodedbackyardofthe21PeachamCrescentpropertywhichslopesintoExbury
ParkandBlackCreek.ThereisatwoͲtierwoodenretainingwallthatsupportsthetableland ofthe
backyard. Thevalleyland conveysBlackCreekandapedestrian pathwayrunsparallelwiththecreek.
Theslopeslippedanddamaged partoftheretainingwallwhichcontinued from23PeachamCrescent. 
Theslipalsocausedthelargetreestofallorleanawayfromtheslope.Additionally, theslopehasbeen
activelyeroding.Minortemporary measures havebeentakenbytheresidentsuchasplacingatarp
overtheexposedsoiltopreventerosion.Basedonthetopographic survey,thesubjectslopeis
approximately 7minheightandextremely steepwithanexistingslopeofapproximately 1.5H:1V.
Existingconditions havebeendocumented andassessedinthefollowing sectionsbasedonfield
observations, geotechnical investigations anddesktopreviewofbackground information obtainedfrom
theTRCA.
2.1. Geotechnical Investigation 
SoilEngineers Ltd.conducted ageotechnical investigation toelaborate ontheexistingsiteconditions 
andproviderecommendations fromageotechnical perspective. One(1)boreholewasdrilledatthetop
ofbankonApril28th,2014toinvestigate thesubsurface soilconditions. Theunderlying soilsconsisted 
of1.5moffill,followedby1.5mofsiltyclay.From3.0mto6.1mbelowthegroundsurfacewassandy
silt.From6.1mto7.6msandysiltandtillwasencountered. From7.6mto9.1msiltyfinesandwas
foundandfollowedbysiltyclayfrom9.1mto10.7m.Lastlyfrom10.7mto11.1mwasfinesand.The
stablegradientinnativesoilisapproximately 2.5H:1V.Thegeotechnical investigation isprovidedin
Appendix B.
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 1 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  21 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
2.2. Underground Services 
SoilEngineers Ltdobtainedunderground serviceslocatesfromOntarioOneCallandaprivatelocatorto
ensurethatthesubjectareawasclearofunderground servicespriortodrillingboreholes. Giventhe
smallsizeofthesiteandcloseproximity oftheboreholes tothesubjectslope,utilitylocatesbeyond
thoseobtainedforthegeotechnical investigation arenotrequired. Thesubjectslopeisclearof
underground services.Correspondence regarding underground servicelocatesisprovidedinAppendix 
C.
2.3. Visual Assessment and Slope Inspection 
ColeEngineering personnel visitedthesiteonApril3rd,April23rdandJune4th,2014toidentifyand
assesssitespecificfactorsthatcouldbecontributing totheslopeinstability aswellashazardsandrisks.
Inaddition,avisualassessment andslopestabilityinspection formwerecompleted fortheproperty. 
Itemizedphotographs takenduringthesiteinvestigation andafterboreholedrillingareprovidedin
Appendix D.
Therearyardof21PeachamCrescenthasmultiplestructures, includingashed,decorative fountain,
stairs,andaretainingwall.Therearandthesideoftheyardaresurrounded bychainlinkfence.
PotentialaccesstothesitewouldbethroughExburyParktotheeastofthesite.
Theproperties alongthesouthsideofPeachamCrescentappeartohavesplitdrainagewherethefront
ofthepropertydrainstothestreetandpickedupbyroadsidecatchbasins andtherearsheetflowinto
thevalleyland. Theslopefacecontainsalargeamountofwoodslabs,debris,andfallentrees(referto
Figure2Ͳ1andFigure2Ͳ2).


2.4. Potential Hazards and Risk 
Theslopefailureisasafetyhazardforthepublicwhomayenterthevalleyland aswellasforthe
residentandvisitorsoftheprivateresidential property. Thereisariskofprivatepropertydamageand
lossoftableland iftheslopecontinues toerode.
Slopefailurehaslefttheslopewithinthepropertyexposedandhasdamaged theexistingretainingwall.
Thiscreatestheriskoffurtherdamagestotheretainingwalls,tableland space,shed,andsafetyfor
residentsandguests.Survivingexistingtreesonthefaceoftheslopeareatriskoffallingiftheslope
continues toerodeasseeninFigure2Ͳ3.
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 3 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  21 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 

Figure2Ͳ3TreeswithinSlopeFailure
3.0 Preliminary Design Concepts 
SoilEngineers Ltd.providedfive(5)potentialalternatives forthesitewhichwereassessedbasedon
feasibility, constructability andcost.Ofthe5alternatives, the“DoNothing”approach wasconsidered 
whichincludesmonitoring ofthesite.Inadditiontothe“DoNothing”approach, fourotheralternatives 
wereinvestigated tomitigaterisktothenearbyhome,restoretheerodedbankandpreventfuture
erosion.
Thealternatives considered areasfollows:
xAlternative #1:DoNothing;
xAlternative #2:Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall;
xAlternative #3:GravityRetaining Wall;
xAlternative #4:SoilAnchors/SoilNails;and,
xAlternative #5:Geoweb.
Itisnoted,theGeowebalternative istypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbe
installedtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodslistedabove.Itisalso
notedsitespecificdetailswillbeprovidedduringthedetaildesignphaseoftheproject.The
geotechnical investigation isprovidedinAppendix Bandthealternatives arediscussed infurtherdetail
below.
3.1. Alternative #1: Do Nothing 
Thefirstproposed alternative istodonothingandleavetheslopeinitscurrentconditions. Theexposed
slopeposesahazardfortheowner,visitors,andthepublicwhomayenterthesite.Ifleftexposed,the
slopewillcontinuetoerodeandrecedetothedetermined LongTermStableSlopeCrest(LTSSC).The
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 4 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  21 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
areabetweentheexistingtopofbankandtheLTSSCwillbeatriskofbeingundermined. This
alternative wouldnotstabilizetheslopeormitigatetheerosionoccurring onthesite.The“DoNothing”
approach isnotdesiredduetotheLTSSCcrossingthroughthefootprintoftheexistingbuilding.TheDo
Nothingapproach includingthelocationoftheLTSSCisillustrated onFigurePHͲ21inAppendix A.
3.2. Alternative #2: Mechanically Stabilized Earth (MSE) Wall  
Thesecondproposed alternative istoconstruct aMechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wallandplantings
initiatingfromthebottomoftheexistingslopeandextending tomatchtheexistinggradeatthetopof
theslope.Significant earthworks arerequiredtoreͲgradetheslopeandrestoreaportionofthetopof
theslopethathaserodedaway.Thealternative willinvolvewrapping layersofstonewithgeogridtoan
inclination of1:1.Theresultingslopefacewillbevegetated andseededtoprovideanaturalized 
exterior.RefertoFigurePHͲ21,DrawingPHͲDCandDrawingDEinAppendix Afortheproposed topof
slopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #2.
3.3. Alternative #3: Gravity Retaining Wall 
Thethirdproposed alternative istoconstruct agravityretainingwallinitiatingattheexistingtopof
slopeandcontinuing downuntilastableslopeisestablished. Thegravitywallcanbeconstructed using
armourstone orotherhardened materialtostabilizetheerodedarea.Significant earthworks are
requiredtoreͲgradetheslopeandconstruct thegravityretainingwall.RefertoFigurePHͲ21and
DrawingDEinAppendix Afortheproposed topofslopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #3.
Giventhesteepness andheightoftheproposed retainingwall,itisrecommended thatthewallbe
fencedofffromthepublicandfromtheresidentsof21PeachamCrescentasasafetyprecaution. Itis
recommended toconsultastructural engineerpriortoimplementing thisalternative. Duetothe
hardened exteriorofthewallanditsimpacttotableland withinthevalleycorridor,thisalternative isnot
recommended whencompared tootheralternatives. 
3.4. Alternative #4: Soil Anchors / Soil Nails 
Thefourthproposed alternative istostabilizetheslopewithuseofsoilanchorsorsoilnailsinitiating
fromthebottomoftheslopeandextending tomatchtheexistinggradeatthetopofslope.The
anchorsareconstructed bylayingapermanent erosioncontrolblanketovertheexistingslope,and
drivinganchorsintotheslopetomaintaintheexistingslopeprofiletoamaximum inclination of1:1.The
resultingslopewillbeseededandvegetated toprovideadditional erosioncontrolandslopestability
whileproviding anaturalized appearance. Itisnoted,thesoilnailalternative istypicallyusedforsurface
erosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbeinstalledtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailure
stabilization methodslistedherein.RefertoFigurePHͲ21,DrawingPHͲDC,andDrawingDEin
Appendix Afortheproposed topofslopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #4.
3.5. Alternative #5: Geoweb System 
Thefifthproposed alternative istostabilizetheslopewiththeuseofageowebsystem.Thegeoweb
systemconsistsofaheavymatthatislaidovertheexistingslopeandanchored inplace,cavitiesinthe
matarethenfilledwithsoilandgranular.Seedsarethenplantedinthecavitiestoassistinsurficial
erosioncontrol.Thisalternative canbeusedonslopesuptoa1:1inclination. Itisnoted,theGeoweb
alternative istypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbeinstalledtogetherwith
otherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodslistedherein.Thetypicaldetailsforthegeoweb
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 5 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  21 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
systemiscombined withthedetailforsoilanchors/soilnailsandisfoundonDrawingPHͲDC,and
DrawingDEinAppendix A.
4.0 Access Considerations 
AccesstositecanbemadefromExburyParkeastoftheproperty. Sometreesmayhavetoberemoved
andthepathwaymayrequirerestoration inordertoreachthesite.Thewoodenretainingwall,
chainlinkfence,andvegetation withintheslopewouldhavetoberemovedtoaccommodate the
construction. Allareasdisturbed throughtheimplementation ofthisalternative willberestoredto
equalͲtoorbetterͲthanexistingcondition; includinganylandscaping featuresonExburyPark.
5.0 Preliminary Cost Estimates 
Asummary ofthecostestimates isbelowinTable5.1.Thecostisanapproximate totalcostacrossthe
neighbouring properties. Itismostlikelythatonealternative willbeselectedforthegroupof
properties, asthedesignwouldtransition mucheasierintotheneighbouring lots.Thetotalestimated 
costisthetotalfor21Ͳ25PeachamCrescent. 
Table5.1–CostEstimateSummary 
Alternative  TotalEstimated Cost
1–DoNothing $0
2–Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall $377,000 
3–GravityRetaining Wall $435,000 
4–SoilAnchors $200,000 
5–GeowebSystem $200,000 
6.0 Alternative Comparison 
Basedonapreliminary reviewofsiteconditions andcostestimates, aproandconcomparison ofthe
alternatives wascompleted andissummarized belowinTable6.1.
Table6.1–Comparison ofAlternatives 
Alternative  Advantages  Disadvantages 

7.0 Conclusions
ColeEngineering staffinvestigated theexistingslopeconditions throughavisualassessment and
topographic survey,andSoilEngineers Ltd.conducted boreholedrillingtoevaluatetheLTSSC.Usingthe
fieldinvestigations, five(5)preliminary alternatives wereproposed basedonfeasibility andtheabilityto
mitigaterisktoinfrastructure, privatepropertyandhumanlife.
Basedontheresultsofthegeotechnical investigation, SoilEngineers Ltd.hasrecommended the
following sloperemediation optionsat21Ͳ25PeachamCrescent: 
xAlternative #2:Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall;
xAlternative #3:GravityRetaining Wall;
xAlternative #4:SoilAnchors/SoilNails;and,
xAlternative #5:Geoweb.
Itisnoted,Alternative #5:Geowebistypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbe
installedtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodsaslistedabove.The
typicaldetailsfortherecommended alternatives areincludedonDrawingPHͲDCandDrawingDEin
Appendix A.

APPENDIX B
Geotechnical Investigation 


 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 41 
 
 
       
21, 23 and 25 PEACHAM CRESCENT 
 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 42 
 
The 3 residential properties are located on the south side of Peacham Crescent, along the 
northern bank of the valley and trail system.  Tableland features include grass lawns, a shed at House No. 21, retaining walls and fence lines at the top of slope.  The houses are approximately 10 to 15 m from the existing top of bank.  
Subsurface Condition (Boreholes 28, 29, 27S to 29S)  
Beneath a layer of topsoil fill, 15± cm thick, and a layer of earth fill extending to depths of 0.8± m and 1.5± m, the site is underlain by a complex stratigraphy consisting of generally very stiff silty clay and clay till and dense sandy silt till, interstratified with layers of compact to dense sandy silt, compact to very dense silty fine sand and very dense fine sand.  The earth fill consists of mainly silty clay and sandy silt material, with some topsoil inclusions and roots.  Groundwater was detected in 1 of the 2 deep boreholes at a depth of 6.7 m (El. 148.3 m) upon completion of the field work.  When measured again one month later, the groundwater level had risen to a depth of 5.4 m (El. 149.6 m).  Sample examinations reveal that the sands found in the lower stratigraphy are generally wet and water-bearing.  
Slope Condition 
The slope height is approximately 8± m, with an overall slope gradient ranging from 
1V:1.19 to 1.27H±, and local gradients of 1V:0.58 to 3.46H±.  The creek, located approximately 5 m away from the existing toe of slope, is channeled and protected on both sides by gabion baskets.  The slope face is wooded, with mature trees and shrubs. Majority of the trees are standing in an upright position, with the exception of some leaning trees where erosion scarring has occurred.  Deep-seated failure was observed near House Nos. 23 and 25 at the crest of the slope.  Exposed tree roots were observed and surface sloughing is evident along steep sections.  The retaining structures and 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 43 
fences are failing, or have already failed. 
 
Slope Stability Analysis and Remediation  
Based on the soil densities revealed by the borehole information, the following soil 
strength parameters were selected for the slope stability analyses.    Soil Strength Parameters

Cross-Section ‘A’ – No. 21 0.957 1.551 - 1V:2.4H 11.5 m 
Cross-Section ‘B’ – No. 23 1.173 1.559 - 1V:2.3H 8 m 
Cross-Section ‘C’ – No. 25 1.269 1.617 - 1V:2.0H 7.5 m 
 
The results indicate that the stability of the existing slopes at Cross-Sections ‘A’ to ‘C’, with a FOS ranging from 0.957 to 1.269, does not satisfy the OMNR guideline requirements for active land use (minimum FOS 1.5).  The stability of these slopes is therefore considered to be geotechnically unacceptable for long-term residential usage.  In order to establish a stable slope, geotechnically stable gradients of 1V:2.0 to 2.4H are recommended for use in native soils.  In earth fill, a gradient of 1V:2.5H minimum should be retained.  The remodeled slopes, yielding a FOS of 1.5+, meet the OMNR requirements.    Toe erosion setback is not required since the watercourse is contained within a functional channel lined with gabion baskets at a distance from the toe of slope.  Based on the analyses results, the following slope stabilization options are recommended for the subject properties.

Statement of Limiting Conditions and Assumptions 
1. This Report/Study (the “Work”) has been prepared at th e request of, and for the exclusive use of, the Owner, and its 
affiliates (the “Intended Users”).  No one other than the Intended Users has the right to use and rely on the Work without 
first obtaining the written authorization of Cole Engineering Group Ltd. (Cole Engineering) and its Owner.   
2. Cole Engineering expressly excludes liability to any party except the Intended Users for any use of, and/or reliance upon, 
the Work.   
3. Cole Engineering notes that the following assumptions were made in completing the Work:   
a) the land use description(s) supplied to us are correct; 
b) the surveys and data supplied to Cole Engineering  by the Owner are accurate;  
c) market timing, approval delivery and secondary source information is within the control of Parties other than Cole 
Engineering; and 
d) there are no encroachments, leases, covenants, binding agreements, restrictions, pledges, charges, liens or special 
assessments outstanding, or encumbrances which would significantly affect the use or servicing. 
Investigations have not been carried out to verify these assumptions.  Cole Engineering deems the sources of data and 
statistical information contained herein to be reliable, but we extend no guarantee of accuracy in these respects.  
4. Cole Engineering accepts no responsibility for legal interpretations, questions of survey, opinion of title, hidden or 
inconspicuous conditions of the property, toxic wastes or contaminated materials, soil or sub-soil conditions, environmental, 
engineering or other factual and technical matters disclosed by the Owner, the Client, or any public agency, which by their 
nature, may change the outcome of the Work.  Such factors, beyond the scope of this Work, could affect the findings, 
conclusions and opinions rendered in the Work.  We have made disclosure of related potential problems that have come to our attention.  Responsibility for diligence with respect to all matt ers of fact reported herein rests with the Intended Users.
5. Cole Engineering practices engineering in the general areas of infrastructure and transportation.  It is not qualified to an d is 
not providing legal or planning advice in this Work.   
6. The legal description of the property and the area of the site were based upon surveys and data supplied to us by the Owner.
The plans, photographs, and sketches contained in this report are included solely to aide in visualizing the location of the 
property, the configuration and boundaries of the site, and the relative position of the improvements on the said lands. 
7. We have made investigations from secondary sources as documented in the Work, but we have not checked for compliance 
with by-laws, codes, agency and governmental regulations, etc., unless specifically noted in the Work. 
8. Because conditions, including capacity, allocation, economic, social, and political factors change rapidly and, on occasion,
without notice or warning, the findings of the Work expressed herein, are as of the date of the Work and cannot necessarily 
be relied upon as of any other date without subsequent advice from Cole Engineering.

outlined in the body of this Work.  Any cost estimates set out in the Work are based on construction averages and subject to

23 PEACHAM CRESCENT 
23 PEACHAM CRESCENT  
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  23 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
1.0 Introduction 
1.1. Location
Thesubjectsiteislocatedattherearof23PeachamCrescentintheCityofToronto,southofthe
intersection ofExburyRoadandPeachamCrescent, westofJaneStreet.Itisnotedtheneighbouring 
properties at21and25PeachamCrescentarealsoincludedinthestudy.23PeachamCrescentisa
privatelyownedresidential lot.ThesubjectsiteislocatedonthesouthsideofPeachamCrescentandis
boundedby21and25PeachamCrescenttotheeastandwest,ExburyParkandBlackCreektothesouth
andPeachamCrescenttothenorth.
AlocationplanisprovidedasFigureLOCͲPHinAppendix A.
2.0 Existing Conditions 
Thesiteconsistsofanerodedbackyardofthe23PeachamCrescentpropertywhichslopesdeepintothe
valley.Thevalleyland conveysBlackCreekandapedestrian pathwayrunsparallelwiththecreek.The
slopehasbeenactivelyerodingandalargeslopefailureisevidentwhichhascausedtreestofallover.
Basedonthetopographic survey,thesubjectslopeisapproximately 9mhighandverysteepwithan
existingslopeofapproximately 1.7H:1V.
Existingconditions havebeendocumented andassessedinthefollowing sectionsbasedonfield
observations, geotechnical investigations anddesktopreviewofbackground information obtainedfrom
theTRCA.
2.1. Geotechnical Investigation 
SoilEngineers Ltd.conducted ageotechnical investigation toelaborate ontheexistingsiteconditions 
andproviderecommendations fromageotechnical perspective. One(1)boreholewasdrilledatthetop
ofbankonApril28th,2014toinvestigate thesubsurface soilconditions. Theunderlying soilsconsisted 
of1.5moffill,followedby1.5mofsiltyclay.From3.0mto6.1mbelowthegroundsurfacewassandy
silt.From6.1mto7.6msandysiltandtillwasencountered. From7.6mto9.1msiltyfinesandwas
foundandfollowedbysiltyclayfrom9.1mto10.7m.Lastlyfrom10.7mto11.1mwasfinesand.The
stablegradientinnativesoilisapproximately 2.3H:1V.Thegeotechnical investigation isprovidedin
Appendix B.
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 1 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  23 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
2.2. Underground Services 
SoilEngineers Ltdobtainedunderground serviceslocatesfromOntarioOneCallandaprivatelocatorto
ensurethatthesubjectareawasclearofunderground servicespriortodrillingboreholes. Giventhe
smallsizeofthesiteandcloseproximity oftheboreholes tothesubjectslope,utilitylocatesbeyond
thoseobtainedforthegeotechnical investigation arenotrequired. Thesubjectslopeisclearof
underground services.Correspondence regarding underground servicelocatesisprovidedinAppendix 
C.
2.3. Visual Assessment and Slope Inspection 
ColeEngineering personnel visitedthesiteonApril3rd,April23rdandJune4th,2014toidentifyand
assesssitespecificfactorsthatcouldbecontributing totheslopeinstability aswellashazardsandrisks.
Inaddition,avisualassessment andslopeinspection formwerecompleted fortheproperty. Itemized
photographs takenduringthesiteinvestigation andafterboreholedrillingareprovidedinAppendix D.
Therearyardof23PeachamCrescenthasmultiplestructures includingagazebo,retainingwall,
decorative fence,andasmallswingset.OntheApril3rdsitevisit,theresidentinformed Cole
Engineering StaffthatpriortotheJuly8thstorm,ashedwaslocatedinthesoutheast cornerofthe
property. Theresidentinformed staffthattheshedwasremovedasitwasdamaged andwasasafety
concernforhimself,guests,andthepublicwhousethetrailatthebottomofslope.Therearandsideof
theyardaresurrounded bychainlinkfence,andadecorative woodenfenceislocatedatthetopof
slide.PotentialaccesstothesitewouldbethroughExburyParktotheeast.
Theproperties alongthesouthsideofPeachamCrescentappeartohavesplitdrainagewherethefront
ofthepropertydrainstothestreetandpickedupbyroadsidecatchbasins andtherearsheetflowsinto
thevalleyland. Thesoilintheslippedareahadnovegetative coverandappeared tobeactivelyeroding
(refertoFigure2Ͳ1).OntheJune4thsitevisit,thetopofslopewastemporarily remediated bythe
residenttohaveasmallvegetable garden(refertoFigure2Ͳ2).

Figure2Ͳ1ErodingSlope



investigation formcompleted forthepropertyisprovidedinAppendix D.
2.4. Potential Hazards and Risk 
Theslopefailureisasafetyhazardforthepublicwhomayenterthevalleyland aswellasforthe
residentandvisitorsoftheprivateresidential property. Thereisariskofprivatepropertydamageand
lossoftableland iftheslopecontinues toerode.
Slopefailurehascausedtheexistingretainingwall,trees,tableland space,chainlinkfence,andshedto
bedamaged orlost.Thiscreatestheriskofdamageandlossofaportionoftheretainingwall.Most
treesonthefaceoftheslopefellintheslideandtheremaining treesleanawayfromtheslopeasseen
inFigure2Ͳ3.

Figure2Ͳ3FailedRetaining WallandFallenTrees
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 3 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  23 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
3.0 Preliminary Design Concepts  
SoilEngineers Ltd.providedfive(5)potentialalternatives forthesitewhichwereassessedbasedon
feasibility, constructability andcost.Ofthe5alternatives, the“DoNothing”approach wasconsidered 
whichincludesmonitoring ofthesite.Inadditiontothe“DoNothing”approach, fourotheralternatives 
wereinvestigated tomitigaterisktothenearbyhome,restoretheerodedbankandpreventfuture
erosion.
Thealternatives considered areasfollows:
xAlternative #1:DoNothing;
xAlternative #2:Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall;
xAlternative #3:GravityRetaining Wall;
xAlternative #4:SoilAnchors/SoilNails;and,
xAlternative #5:Geoweb.
Itisnoted,theGeowebalternative istypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbe
installedtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodslistedabove.Itisalso
notedsitespecificdetailswillbeprovidedduringthedetaildesignphaseoftheproject.The
geotechnical investigation isprovidedinAppendix Bandthealternatives arediscussed infurtherdetail
below.
3.1. Alternative #1: Do Nothing 
Thefirstproposed alternative istodonothingandleavetheslopeinitscurrentconditions. Theexposed
slopeposesahazardfortheowner,visitors,andthepublicwhomayenterthesite.Ifleftexposed,the
slopewillcontinuetoerodeandrecedetothedetermined LongTermStableSlopeCrest(LTSSC).The
areabetweentheexistingtopofbankandtheLTSSCwillbeatriskofbeingundermined. This
alternative wouldnotstabilizetheslopeormitigatetheerosionoccurring onthesite.The“DoNothing”
approach isnotdesiredduetotheLTSSCcrossingthroughthefootprintoftheexistingbuilding.TheDo
Nothingapproach includingthelocationoftheLTSSCisillustrated onFigurePHͲ23inAppendix A.
3.2. Alternative #2: Mechanically Stabilized Earth (MSE) Wall  
Thesecondproposed alternative istoconstruct aMechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wallandplantings
initiatingfromthebottomoftheexistingslopeandextending tomatchtheexistinggradeatthetopof
theslope.Significant earthworks arerequiredtoreͲgradetheslopeandrestoreaportionofthetopof
theslopethathaserodedaway.Thealternative willinvolvewrapping layersofstonewithgeogridtoan
inclination of1:1.Theresultingslopefacewillbevegetated andseededtoprovideanaturalized 
exterior.RefertoFigurePH23,DrawingPHͲDCandDrawingDEinAppendix Afortheproposed topof
slopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #2.
3.3. Alternative #3: Gravity Retaining Wall 
Thethirdproposed alternative istoconstruct agravityretainingwallinitiatingattheexistingtopof
slopeandcontinuing downuntilastableslopeisestablished. Thegravitywallcanbeconstructed using
armourstone orotherhardened materialtostabilizetheerodedarea.Significant earthworks are
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 4 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  23 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
requiredtoreͲgradetheslopeandconstruct thegravityretainingwall.RefertoFigurePHͲ23and
DrawingDEinAppendix Afortheproposed topofslopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #3.
Giventhesteepness andheightoftheproposed retainingwall,itisrecommended thatthewallbe
fencedofffromthepublicandfromtheresidentsof23PeachamCrescentasasafetyprecaution. Itis
recommended toconsultastructural engineerpriortoimplementing thisalternative. Duetothe
hardened exteriorofthewallanditsimpacttotableland withinthevalleycorridor,thisalternative isnot
recommended whencompared tootheralternatives. 
3.4. Alternative #4: Soil Anchors / Soil Nails 
Thefourthproposed alternative istostabilizetheslopewithuseofsoilanchorsorsoilnailsinitiating
fromthebottomoftheslopeandextending tomatchtheexistinggradeatthetopofslope.The
anchorsareconstructed bylayingapermanent erosioncontrolblanketovertheexistingslope,and
drivinganchorsintotheslopetomaintaintheexistingslopeprofiletoamaximum inclination of1:1.The
resultingslopewillbeseededandvegetated toprovideadditional erosioncontrolandslopestability
whileproviding anaturalized appearance. Itisnoted,thesoilnailalternative istypicallyusedforsurface
erosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbeinstalledtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailure
stabilization methodslistedherein.RefertoFigurePHͲ23,DrawingPHͲDC,andDrawingDEin
Appendix Afortheproposed topofslopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #4.
3.5. Alternative #5: Geoweb System 
Thefifthproposed alternative istostabilizetheslopewiththeuseofageowebsystem.Thegeoweb
systemconsistsofaheavymatthatislaidovertheexistingslopeandanchored inplace,cavitiesinthe
matarethenfilledwithsoilandgranular.Seedsarethenplantedinthecavitiestoassistinsurficial
erosioncontrol.Thisalternative canbeusedonslopesuptoa1:1inclination. Itisnoted,theGeoweb
alternative istypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbeinstalledtogetherwith
otherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodslistedherein.Thetypicaldetailsforthegeoweb
systemiscombined withthedetailforsoilanchors/soilnailsandisfoundonDrawingPHͲDC,and
DrawingDEinAppendix A.
4.0 Access Considerations 
AccesstositecanbemadefromExburyParkeastoftheproperty. Sometreesmayhavetoberemoved
andthepathwaymayrequirerestoration inordertoreachthesite.Thewoodenretainingwall,
decorative fence,chainlinkfence,andvegetation withintheslopewouldhavetoberemovedto
accommodate theconstruction. Allareasdisturbed throughtheimplementation ofthisalternative will
berestoredtoequalͲtoorbetterͲthanexistingcondition; includinganylandscaping featuresonExbury
Park.
5.0 Preliminary Cost Estimates 
Asummary ofthecostestimates isbelowinTable5.1.Thecostisanapproximate totalcostacrossthe
neighbouring properties. Itismostlikelythatonealternative willbeselectedforthegroupof
properties, asthedesignwouldtransition mucheasierintotheneighbouring lots.Thetotalestimated 
costisthetotalfor21Ͳ25PeachamCrescent.  

6.0 Alternative Comparison 
Basedonapreliminary reviewofsiteconditions andcostestimates, aproandconcomparison ofthe
alternatives wascompleted andissummarized belowinTable6.1.
Table6.1–Comparison ofAlternatives 
Alternative  Advantages  Disadvantages 
1–DoNothing Lowestcost.Unstableslopeisasafetyhazard;and,
Increased probability ofpropertylossif
notrestored.
2–Mechanically 
Stabilized Earth(MSE)
WallMitigates slopestabilityrisk;and,
Facecanbevegetated. Potentialsafetyhazardfromsteep
slopes;
Largescaledisturbance; and,
Reliesonengineered benchedwalls.
3–GravityRetaining 
WallMitigates slopestabilityrisk.Greaterpotentialsafetyhazardfrom
tallerverticalwalls;
Largescaledisturbance; 
Reliesonengineered stonewalls;and,
Highestcostalternative. 
4–SoilAnchors/Soil
NailsMitigates slopestabilityrisk;
Naturalaestheticappeal;
Minimaldisturbance; and,
Relatively lowcost.Smallerfactorofsafety;and,
Reliesongeotechnical investigations 
andlocalsoilconditions. 
5–GeowebSystemMitigates slopestabilityrisk;
Naturalaestheticappeal;
Minimaldisturbance; and,
Relatively lowcost.Smallerfactorofsafety;
Reliesongeotechnical investigations 
andlocalsoilconditions; and,
Requiresadditional slopefailure
stabilization inconjunction with
geowebsystem
7.0 Conclusions
ColeEngineering staffinvestigated theexistingslopeconditions throughavisualassessment and
topographic survey,andSoilEngineers Ltd.conducted boreholedrillingtoevaluatetheLTSSC.Usingthe
fieldinvestigations, five(5)preliminary alternatives wereproposed basedonfeasibility andtheabilityto
mitigaterisktoinfrastructure, privatepropertyandhumanlife.
Basedontheresultsofthegeotechnical investigation, SoilEngineers Ltd.hasrecommended the
following sloperemediation optionsat21Ͳ25PeachamCrescent: 
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 6 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  23 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 7 of 7 
xAlternative #2:Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall;
xAlternative #3:GravityRetaining Wall;
xAlternative #4:SoilAnchors/SoilNails;and,
xAlternative #5:Geoweb.
Itisnoted,Alternative #5:Geowebistypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbe
installedtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodsaslistedabove.The
typicaldetailsfortherecommended alternatives areincludedonDrawingPHͲDCandDrawingDEin
Appendix A.

APPENDIX B
Geotechnical Investigation 


 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 41 
 
 
       
21, 23 and 25 PEACHAM CRESCENT 
 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 42 
 
The 3 residential properties are located on the south side of Peacham Crescent, along the 
northern bank of the valley and trail system.  Tableland features include grass lawns, a shed at House No. 21, retaining walls and fence lines at the top of slope.  The houses are approximately 10 to 15 m from the existing top of bank.  
Subsurface Condition (Boreholes 28, 29, 27S to 29S)  
Beneath a layer of topsoil fill, 15± cm thick, and a layer of earth fill extending to depths of 0.8± m and 1.5± m, the site is underlain by a complex stratigraphy consisting of generally very stiff silty clay and clay till and dense sandy silt till, interstratified with layers of compact to dense sandy silt, compact to very dense silty fine sand and very dense fine sand.  The earth fill consists of mainly silty clay and sandy silt material, with some topsoil inclusions and roots.  Groundwater was detected in 1 of the 2 deep boreholes at a depth of 6.7 m (El. 148.3 m) upon completion of the field work.  When measured again one month later, the groundwater level had risen to a depth of 5.4 m (El. 149.6 m).  Sample examinations reveal that the sands found in the lower stratigraphy are generally wet and water-bearing.  
Slope Condition 
The slope height is approximately 8± m, with an overall slope gradient ranging from 
1V:1.19 to 1.27H±, and local gradients of 1V:0.58 to 3.46H±.  The creek, located approximately 5 m away from the existing toe of slope, is channeled and protected on both sides by gabion baskets.  The slope face is wooded, with mature trees and shrubs. Majority of the trees are standing in an upright position, with the exception of some leaning trees where erosion scarring has occurred.  Deep-seated failure was observed near House Nos. 23 and 25 at the crest of the slope.  Exposed tree roots were observed and surface sloughing is evident along steep sections.  The retaining structures and 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 43 
fences are failing, or have already failed. 
 
Slope Stability Analysis and Remediation  
Based on the soil densities revealed by the borehole information, the following soil 
strength parameters were selected for the slope stability analyses.    Soil Strength Parameters

Cross-Section ‘A’ – No. 21 0.957 1.551 - 1V:2.4H 11.5 m 
Cross-Section ‘B’ – No. 23 1.173 1.559 - 1V:2.3H 8 m 
Cross-Section ‘C’ – No. 25 1.269 1.617 - 1V:2.0H 7.5 m 
 
The results indicate that the stability of the existing slopes at Cross-Sections ‘A’ to ‘C’, with a FOS ranging from 0.957 to 1.269, does not satisfy the OMNR guideline requirements for active land use (minimum FOS 1.5).  The stability of these slopes is therefore considered to be geotechnically unacceptable for long-term residential usage.  In order to establish a stable slope, geotechnically stable gradients of 1V:2.0 to 2.4H are recommended for use in native soils.  In earth fill, a gradient of 1V:2.5H minimum should be retained.  The remodeled slopes, yielding a FOS of 1.5+, meet the OMNR requirements.    Toe erosion setback is not required since the watercourse is contained within a functional channel lined with gabion baskets at a distance from the toe of slope.  Based on the analyses results, the following slope stabilization options are recommended for the subject properties.

Statement of Limiting Conditions and Assumptions 
1. This Report/Study (the “Work”) has been prepared at th e request of, and for the exclusive use of, the Owner, and its 
affiliates (the “Intended Users”).  No one other than the Intended Users has the right to use and rely on the Work without 
first obtaining the written authorization of Cole Engineering Group Ltd. (Cole Engineering) and its Owner.   
2. Cole Engineering expressly excludes liability to any party except the Intended Users for any use of, and/or reliance upon, 
the Work.   
3. Cole Engineering notes that the following assumptions were made in completing the Work:   
a) the land use description(s) supplied to us are correct; 
b) the surveys and data supplied to Cole Engineering  by the Owner are accurate;  
c) market timing, approval delivery and secondary source information is within the control of Parties other than Cole 
Engineering; and 
d) there are no encroachments, leases, covenants, binding agreements, restrictions, pledges, charges, liens or special 
assessments outstanding, or encumbrances which would significantly affect the use or servicing. 
Investigations have not been carried out to verify these assumptions.  Cole Engineering deems the sources of data and 
statistical information contained herein to be reliable, but we extend no guarantee of accuracy in these respects.  
4. Cole Engineering accepts no responsibility for legal interpretations, questions of survey, opinion of title, hidden or 
inconspicuous conditions of the property, toxic wastes or contaminated materials, soil or sub-soil conditions, environmental, 
engineering or other factual and technical matters disclosed by the Owner, the Client, or any public agency, which by their 
nature, may change the outcome of the Work.  Such factors, beyond the scope of this Work, could affect the findings, 
conclusions and opinions rendered in the Work.  We have made disclosure of related potential problems that have come to our attention.  Responsibility for diligence with respect to all matt ers of fact reported herein rests with the Intended Users.
5. Cole Engineering practices engineering in the general areas of infrastructure and transportation.  It is not qualified to an d is 
not providing legal or planning advice in this Work.

The plans, photographs, and sketches contained in this report are included solely to aide in visualizing the location of the 
property, the configuration and boundaries of the site, and the relative position of the improvements on the said lands.

with by-laws, codes, agency and governmental regulations, etc., unless specifically noted in the Work.

without notice or warning, the findings of the Work expressed herein, are as of the date of the Work and cannot necessarily 
be relied upon as of any other date without subsequent advice from Cole Engineering.

25 PEACHAM CRESCENT 
25 PEACHAM CRESCENT   
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  25 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
1.0 Introduction 
1.1. Location
Thesubjectsiteislocatedattherearof25PeachamCrescentintheCityofToronto,southofthe
intersection ofExburyRoadandPeachamCrescent, westofJaneStreet.Itisnotedtheneighbouring 
propertyat23PeachamCrescentaswellas21PeachamCrescentarealsoincludedinthestudy.25
PeachamCrescentisaprivatelyownedresidential lot.Thesubjectsiteislocatedonthesouthsideof
PeachamCrescenttoandisboundedby23and27PeachamCrescenttotheeastandwest,ExburyPark
andBlackCreekthesouthandPeachamCrescenttothenorth.
AlocationplanisprovidedasFigureLOCͲPHinAppendix A.
2.0 Existing Conditions 
Thesiteconsistsofanerodedbackyardofthe25PeachamCrescentpropertywhichslopesdeepintothe
valley.Thevalleyland conveysBlackCreekandapedestrian pathwayrunsparallelwiththecreek.A
patioextendsfromthehouseandawoodenretainingwallisconstructed withintheslopeatthesouth
limitoftheproperty. Theslopehasbeenslippedatthesoutheast corneroftheproperty, damaging the
woodenretainingwall.Basedonthetopographic survey,thesubjectslopeisapproximately 7mhigh
andverysteepwithanexistingslopeofapproximately 1.3H:1V.
Existingconditions havebeendocumented andassessedinthefollowing sectionsbasedonfield
observations, geotechnical investigations anddesktopreviewofbackground information obtainedfrom
theTRCA.
2.1. Geotechnical Investigation 
SoilEngineers Ltd.conducted ageotechnical investigation toelaborate ontheexistingsiteconditions 
andproviderecommendations fromageotechnical perspective. One(1)boreholewasdrilledatthetop
ofbankonApril25th,2014toinvestigate thesubsurface soilconditions. Theunderlying soilsconsisted 
of1.5moffill,followedby6.1mofsandysiltandtill.From7.6mto10.7mbelowthegroundwassilty
clayandtill.From10.7mto11.1msiltyfinesandwasencountered. Thestablegradientinnativesoilis
approximately 2.2H:1V.Thegeotechnical investigation isprovidedinAppendix B.
2.2. Underground Services 
SoilEngineers Ltdobtainedunderground serviceslocatesfromOntarioOneCallandaprivatelocatorto
ensurethatthesubjectareawasclearofunderground servicespriortodrillingboreholes. Giventhe
smallsizeofthesiteandcloseproximity oftheboreholes tothesubjectslope,utilitylocatesbeyond
thoseobtainedforthegeotechnical investigation arenotrequired. Thesubjectslopeisclearof
underground services.Correspondence regarding underground servicelocatesisprovidedinAppendix 
C.
2.3. Visual Assessment and Slope Inspection 
ColeEngineering personnel visitedthesiteonApril3rd,April23rdandJune4th,2014toidentifyand
assesssitespecificfactorsthatcouldbecontributing totheslopeinstability aswellashazardsandrisks.
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 1 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  25 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
Inaddition,avisualassessment andslopeinspection formwerecompleted fortheproperty. Itemized
photographs takenduringthesiteinvestigation andafterboreholedrillingareprovidedinAppendix D.
Therearyardof25PeachamCrescenthasaconcretepatioextending fromthehouseandachainlink
fencesurrounding therearandsidesoftheyard.PotentialaccesstothesitewouldbefromExburyPark
totheeastofthesite.
Theproperties alongthesouthsideofPeachamCrescentappeartohavesplitdrainagewherethefront
ofthepropertydrainstothestreetandpickedupbyroadsidecatchbasins andtherearsheetflowinto
thevalleyland. Theslopeattheedgeofthebackyardhasslippedandcauseddamagetothewooden
retainingwallandchainlinkfence.(refertoFigure2Ͳ1).Inaddition,theremaining retainingwall
structurehasdoesnotappearstableandmayadditionally fail(refertoFigure2Ͳ2).

Figure2Ͳ1FailedSlopeandDamaged Retaining Wall



Fieldinvestigation formsandsketcheswereprepared aspartofthevisualassessments. Thefield
investigation formcompleted forthepropertyisprovidedinAppendix D.
2.4. Potential Hazards and Risk 
Theslopefailureisasafetyhazardforthepublicwhomayenterthevalleyland aswellasforthe
residentandvisitorsoftheprivateresidential property. Thereisariskofprivatepropertydamageand
lossoftableland iftheslopecontinues toerode.
Slopefailurehaslefttheeastsideoftheslopewithinthepropertytobeexposedandtheexisting
retainingwalldamaged. Thiscreatestheriskoflossoftheremainder oftheretainingwall,tableland 
space,aswellasasafetyhazardtotheresidentsandvisitorstotheproperty(refertoFigure2Ͳ3).
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  25 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 

Figure2Ͳ3SlopeHeldbyRemaining Retaining Wall
3.0 Preliminary Design Concepts  
SoilEngineers Ltd.providedfive(5)potentialalternatives forthesitewhichwereassessedbasedon
feasibility, constructability andcost.Ofthe5alternatives, the“DoNothing”approach wasconsidered 
whichincludesmonitoring ofthesite.Inadditiontothe“DoNothing”approach, fourotheralternatives 
wereinvestigated tomitigaterisktothenearbyhome,restoretheerodedbankandpreventfuture
erosion.
Thealternatives considered areasfollows:
xAlternative #1:DoNothing;
xAlternative #2:Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall;
xAlternative #3:GravityRetaining Wall;
xAlternative #4:SoilAnchors/SoilNails;and,
xAlternative #5:Geoweb.
Itisnoted,theGeowebalternative istypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbe
installedtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodslistedabove.Itisalso
notedsitespecificdetailswillbeprovidedduringthedetaildesignphaseoftheproject.The
geotechnical investigation isprovidedinAppendix Bandthealternatives arediscussed infurtherdetail
below.
3.1. Alternative #1: Do Nothing 
Thefirstproposed alternative istodonothingandleavetheslopeinitscurrentconditions. Theexposed
slopeposesahazardfortheowner,visitors,andthepublicwhomayenterthesite.Ifleftexposed,the
slopewillcontinuetoerodeandrecedetothedetermined LongTermStableSlopeCrest(LTSSC).The
areabetweentheexistingtopofbankandtheLTSSCwillbeatriskofbeingundermined. This
alternative wouldnotstabilizetheslopeormitigatetheerosionoccurring onthesite.The“DoNothing”
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 4 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  25 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
approach isnotdesiredduetotheLTSSCcrossingthroughthefootprintoftheexistingbuilding.TheDo
Nothingapproach includingthelocationoftheLTSSCisillustrated onFigurePHͲ25inAppendix A.
3.2. Alternative #2: Mechanically Stabilized Earth (MSE) Wall  
Thesecondproposed alternative istoconstruct aMechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wallandplantings
initiatingfromthebottomoftheexistingslopeandextending tomatchtheexistinggradeatthetopof
theslope.Significant earthworks arerequiredtoreͲgradetheslopeandrestoreaportionofthetopof
theslopethathaserodedaway.Thealternative willinvolvewrapping layersofstonewithgeogridtoan
inclination of1:1.Theresultingslopefacewillbevegetated andseededtoprovideanaturalized 
exterior.RefertoFigurePHͲ25,DrawingPHͲDCandDrawingDEinAppendix Afortheproposed topof
slopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #2.
3.3. Alternative #3: Gravity Retaining Wall 
Thethirdproposed alternative istoconstruct agravityretainingwallinitiatingattheexistingtopof
slopeandcontinuing downuntilastableslopeisestablished. Thegravitywallcanbeconstructed using
armourstone orotherhardened materialtostabilizetheerodedarea.Significant earthworks are
requiredtoreͲgradetheslopeandconstruct thegravityretainingwall.RefertoFigurePHͲ25and
DrawingDEinAppendix Afortheproposed topofslopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #3.
Giventhesteepness andheightoftheproposed retainingwall,itisrecommended thatthewallbe
fencedofffromthepublicandfromtheresidentsof25PeachamCrescentasasafetyprecaution. Itis
recommended toconsultastructural engineerpriortoimplementing thisalternative. Duetothe
hardened exteriorofthewallanditsimpacttotableland withinthevalleycorridor,thisalternative isnot
recommended whencompared tootheralternatives. 
3.4. Alternative #4: Soil Anchors / Soil Nails 
Thefourthproposed alternative istostabilizetheslopewithuseofsoilanchorsorsoilnailsinitiating
fromthebottomoftheslopeandextending tomatchtheexistinggradeatthetopofslope.The
anchorsareconstructed bylayingapermanent erosioncontrolblanketovertheexistingslope,and
drivinganchorsintotheslopetomaintaintheexistingslopeprofiletoamaximum inclination of1:1.The
resultingslopewillbeseededandvegetated toprovideadditional erosioncontrolandslopestability
whileproviding anaturalized appearance. Itisnoted,thesoilnailalternative istypicallyusedforsurface
erosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbeinstalledtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailure
stabilization methodslistedherein.RefertoFigurePHͲ25,DrawingPHͲDC,andDrawingDEin
Appendix Afortheproposed topofslopealignment andatypicaldetailofAlternative #4.
3.5. Alternative #5: Geoweb System 
Thefifthproposed alternative istostabilizetheslopewiththeuseofageowebsystem.Thegeoweb
systemconsistsofaheavymatthatislaidovertheexistingslopeandanchored inplace,cavitiesinthe
matarethenfilledwithsoilandgranular.Seedsarethenplantedinthecavitiestoassistinsurficial
erosioncontrol.Thisalternative canbeusedonslopesuptoa1:1inclination. Itisnoted,theGeoweb
alternative istypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbeinstalledtogetherwith
otherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodslistedherein.Thetypicaldetailsforthegeoweb
systemiscombined withthedetailforsoilanchors/soilnailsandisfoundonDrawingPHͲDC,and
DrawingDEinAppendix A.
WR14-0072 (April 2015) Page 5 of 7 

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority  25 Peacham Crescent 
City of Toronto  Slope Stability & Erosion Risk Assessment 
4.0 Access Considerations 
AccesstositecanbemadefromExburyParkeastoftheproperty. Sometreesmayhavetoberemoved
andthepathwaymayrequirerestoration inordertoreachthesite.Thewoodenretainingwall,
chainlinkfence,andvegetation withintheslopewouldhavetoberemovedtoaccommodate the
construction. Allareasdisturbed throughtheimplementation ofthisalternative willberestoredto
equalͲtoorbetterͲthanexistingcondition; includinganylandscaping featuresonExburyPark.
5.0 Preliminary Cost Estimates 
Asummary ofthecostestimates isbelowinTable5.1.Thecostisanapproximate totalcostacrossthe
neighbouring properties. Itismostlikelythatonealternative willbeselectedforthegroupof
properties, asthedesignwouldtransition mucheasierintotheneighbouring lots.Thetotalestimated 
costisthetotalfor21Ͳ25PeachamCrescent. 
Table5.1–CostEstimateSummary 
Alternative  TotalEstimated Cost
1–DoNothing $0
2–Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall $377,000 
3–GravityRetaining Wall $435,000 
4–SoilAnchors $200,000 
5–GeowebSystem $200,000 
6.0 Alternative Comparison 
Basedonapreliminary reviewofsiteconditions andcostestimates, aproandconcomparison ofthe
alternatives wascompleted andissummarized belowinTable6.1.
Table6.1–Comparison ofAlternatives 
Alternative  Advantages  Disadvantages 
1–DoNothing Lowestcost.Unstableslopeisasafetyhazard;and,
Increased probability ofpropertylossif
notrestored.
2–Mechanically 
Stabilized Earth(MSE)
WallMitigates slopestabilityrisk;and,
Facecanbevegetated. Potentialsafetyhazardfromsteep
slopes;
Largescaledisturbance; and,
Reliesonengineered benchedwalls.
3–GravityRetaining 
WallMitigates slopestabilityrisk.Greaterpotentialsafetyhazardfrom
tallerverticalwalls;
Largescaledisturbance; 
Reliesonengineered stonewalls;and,
Highestcostalternative. 

NailsMitigates slopestabilityrisk;
Naturalaestheticappeal;
Minimaldisturbance; and,
Relatively lowcost.Smallerfactorofsafety;and,

7.0 Conclusions and Recommendations 
ColeEngineering staffinvestigated theexistingslopeconditions throughavisualassessment and
topographic survey,andSoilEngineers Ltd.conducted boreholedrillingtoevaluatetheLTSSC.Usingthe
fieldinvestigations, five(5)preliminary alternatives wereproposed basedonfeasibility andtheabilityto
mitigaterisktoinfrastructure, privatepropertyandhumanlife.
Basedontheresultsofthegeotechnical investigation, SoilEngineers Ltd.hasrecommended the
following sloperemediation optionsat21Ͳ25PeachamCrescent: 
xAlternative #2:Mechanically Stabilized Earth(MSE)Wall;
xAlternative #3:GravityRetaining Wall;
xAlternative #4:SoilAnchors/SoilNails;and,
xAlternative #5:Geoweb.
Itisnoted,Alternative #5:Geowebistypicallyusedforsurfaceerosioncontrolandtherefore shouldbe
installedtogetherwithotherdeepͲseatedslopefailurestabilization methodsaslistedabove.The
typicaldetailsfortherecommended alternatives areincludedonDrawingPHͲDCandDrawingDEin
Appendix A.

APPENDIX B
Geotechnical Investigation 


 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 41 
 
 
       
21, 23 and 25 PEACHAM CRESCENT 
 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 42 
 
The 3 residential properties are located on the south side of Peacham Crescent, along the 
northern bank of the valley and trail system.  Tableland features include grass lawns, a shed at House No. 21, retaining walls and fence lines at the top of slope.  The houses are approximately 10 to 15 m from the existing top of bank.  
Subsurface Condition (Boreholes 28, 29, 27S to 29S)  
Beneath a layer of topsoil fill, 15± cm thick, and a layer of earth fill extending to depths of 0.8± m and 1.5± m, the site is underlain by a complex stratigraphy consisting of generally very stiff silty clay and clay till and dense sandy silt till, interstratified with layers of compact to dense sandy silt, compact to very dense silty fine sand and very dense fine sand.  The earth fill consists of mainly silty clay and sandy silt material, with some topsoil inclusions and roots.  Groundwater was detected in 1 of the 2 deep boreholes at a depth of 6.7 m (El. 148.3 m) upon completion of the field work.  When measured again one month later, the groundwater level had risen to a depth of 5.4 m (El. 149.6 m).  Sample examinations reveal that the sands found in the lower stratigraphy are generally wet and water-bearing.  
Slope Condition 
The slope height is approximately 8± m, with an overall slope gradient ranging from 
1V:1.19 to 1.27H±, and local gradients of 1V:0.58 to 3.46H±.  The creek, located approximately 5 m away from the existing toe of slope, is channeled and protected on both sides by gabion baskets.  The slope face is wooded, with mature trees and shrubs. Majority of the trees are standing in an upright position, with the exception of some leaning trees where erosion scarring has occurred.  Deep-seated failure was observed near House Nos. 23 and 25 at the crest of the slope.  Exposed tree roots were observed and surface sloughing is evident along steep sections.  The retaining structures and 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 43 
fences are failing, or have already failed. 
 
Slope Stability Analysis and Remediation  
Based on the soil densities revealed by the borehole information, the following soil 
strength parameters were selected for the slope stability analyses.    Soil Strength Parameters

Cross-Section ‘A’ – No. 21 0.957 1.551 - 1V:2.4H 11.5 m 
Cross-Section ‘B’ – No. 23 1.173 1.559 - 1V:2.3H 8 m 
Cross-Section ‘C’ – No. 25 1.269 1.617 - 1V:2.0H 7.5 m 
 
The results indicate that the stability of the existing slopes at Cross-Sections ‘A’ to ‘C’, with a FOS ranging from 0.957 to 1.269, does not satisfy the OMNR guideline requirements for active land use (minimum FOS 1.5).  The stability of these slopes is therefore considered to be geotechnically unacceptable for long-term residential usage.  In order to establish a stable slope, geotechnically stable gradients of 1V:2.0 to 2.4H are recommended for use in native soils.  In earth fill, a gradient of 1V:2.5H minimum should be retained.  The remodeled slopes, yielding a FOS of 1.5+, meet the OMNR requirements.    Toe erosion setback is not required since the watercourse is contained within a functional channel lined with gabion baskets at a distance from the toe of slope.  Based on the analyses results, the following slope stabilization options are recommended for the subject properties.

APPENDIX E
Statement OfLimitingConditions 
Statement of Limiting Conditions and Assumptions 
1. This Report/Study (the “Work”) has been prepared at th e request of, and for the exclusive use of, the Owner, and its 
affiliates (the “Intended Users”).  No one other than the Intended Users has the right to use and rely on the Work without 
first obtaining the written authorization of Cole Engineering Group Ltd. (Cole Engineering) and its Owner.   
2. Cole Engineering expressly excludes liability to any party except the Intended Users for any use of, and/or reliance upon, 
the Work.   
3. Cole Engineering notes that the following assumptions were made in completing the Work:   
a) the land use description(s) supplied to us are correct; 
b) the surveys and data supplied to Cole Engineering  by the Owner are accurate;  
c) market timing, approval delivery and secondary source information is within the control of Parties other than Cole 
Engineering; and 
d) there are no encroachments, leases, covenants, binding agreements, restrictions, pledges, charges, liens or special 
assessments outstanding, or encumbrances which would significantly affect the use or servicing. 
Investigations have not been carried out to verify these assumptions.  Cole Engineering deems the sources of data and 
statistical information contained herein to be reliable, but we extend no guarantee of accuracy in these respects.  
4. Cole Engineering accepts no responsibility for legal interpretations, questions of survey, opinion of title, hidden or 
inconspicuous conditions of the property, toxic wastes or contaminated materials, soil or sub-soil conditions, environmental, 
engineering or other factual and technical matters disclosed by the Owner, the Client, or any public agency, which by their 
nature, may change the outcome of the Work.  Such factors, beyond the scope of this Work, could affect the findings, 
conclusions and opinions rendered in the Work.  We have made disclosure of related potential problems that have come to our attention.  Responsibility for diligence with respect to all matt ers of fact reported herein rests with the Intended Users.
5. Cole Engineering practices engineering in the general areas of infrastructure and transportation.  It is not qualified to an d is 
not providing legal or planning advice in this Work.   
6. The legal description of the property and the area of the site were based upon surveys and data supplied to us by the Owner.
The plans, photographs, and sketches contained in this report are included solely to aide in visualizing the location of the 
property, the configuration and boundaries of the site, and the relative position of the improvements on the said lands. 
7. We have made investigations from secondary sources as documented in the Work, but we have not checked for compliance 
with by-laws, codes, agency and governmental regulations, etc., unless specifically noted in the Work. 
8. Because conditions, including capacity, allocation, economic, social, and political factors change rapidly and, on occasion,
without notice or warning, the findings of the Work expressed herein, are as of the date of the Work and cannot necessarily 
be relied upon as of any other date without subsequent advice from Cole Engineering. 
9. The value of proposed improvements should be applied only with regard to the purpose and function of the Work, as 
outlined in the body of this Work.  Any cost estimates set out in the Work are based on construction averages and subject to 
change. 
10. Neither possession of the Work, nor a copy of it, carries the right of publication.  All copyright in the Work is reserved to
Cole Engineering.  The Work shall not be disclosed, produced or reproduced, quoted from, or referred to, in whole or in 
part, or published in any manner, without the express written consent of Cole Engineering and the Owner. 
11. The Work is only valid if it bears the professional engineer’s seal and original signature of the author, and if considered  in 
its entirety.  Responsibility for unauthorized alteration to the Work is denied.

   1.0  INTRODUCTION  
 In accordance with Purchase Order No. 2170-14, dated April 21, 2014, from Mr. Mark Bassingthwaite of Cole Engineering Group Ltd., a soil investigation was carried out at various properties across the Area E - Black Creek Sub-Watershed study area, City of Toronto.     The severe thunderstorm on July 8, 2013, brought large amounts of precipitation and flooding across the Greater Toronto Area, resulting in bank erosion, slope and retaining wall failures at various properties.  The purpose of the investigation was to reveal the subsurface conditions in order to assess the slope stability and risk of erosion of the existing valley slopes within the study area, and to develop preliminary stabilization options.   
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 2 
 
   2.0  FIELD WORK  
 The field work, consisting of 19 deep boreholes to depths ranging from 9.3 to 14.2 m and 28 shallow boreholes to depths of 1.5 to 4.6 m, was performed between April 25 and May 26, 2014, at the locations shown on individual site plans, enclosed.  A suffix ‘S’ on the borehole log denotes shallow boreholes, performed mainly in the rear yard to assess the earth fill depth and quality.  The deep boreholes were advanced at intervals to the sampling depths by a track-mounted machine with continuous-flight power-auger equipped for soil sampling.  Standard Penetration Tests, using the procedures described on the enclosed “List of Abbreviations and Terms”, were performed at the sampling depths.  Due to access restrictions, the shallow boreholes were carried out manually using the weight of a  70 lb. drop hammer and the penetration tests were performed continuously with depth.    The test results are recorded as the Standard Penetration Resistance (or ‘N’ values) of the subsoil.  The relative density of the granular strata and the consistency of the cohesive strata are inferred from the ‘N’ values.  Split-spoon samples were recovered for soil classification and laboratory testing.  Thirteen 25-mm diameter groundwater monitoring wells were installed in selected deep boreholes.  They were constructed using 1.5 m slotted screen and riser pipes, backfilled with the appropriate filtering sand material, sealed with bentonite, and protected by a flush-mount protective casing.   Detailed descriptions of the encountered subsurface conditions and the depths of the monitoring wells are presented on the Borehole Logs, comprising Figures 1 to 60, inclusive.  The elevation at each of the borehole locations was surveyed using handheld 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 3 
Global Navigation Satellite System survey equipment with a maximum accuracy of 0.1± 
m.
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 4 
 
3.0  SLOPE STABILITY ANALYSIS  
 The study area, Area E, encompasses 30 residential properties located along 10 municipal streets within the Black Creek sub-watershed.  Borehole investigation was not conducted at 2 of the 30 properties due to denial of permission to enter.  The following section is an account of the site description, revealed subsurface condition, existing slope information including overall height, slope gradients and conditions, slope stability analyses and results, and recommended remediation options for each property, organized by street address.      Detailed subsoil information is documented on the attached borehole logs.  Grain size analyses were performed on 4 different soil types, namely silty clay till, silty clay, silt and fine to medium sand.  The gradations are plotted on Figures 61 to 65, enclosed in Appendix A.  For the stability analysis, the existing slope cross-section profiles were interpolated from the contours and section drawings provided by Cole Engineering Group Ltd.  The subsurface profile is interpreted from the deep and shallow Borehole Logs, selected based on their proximity to the analyzed section.  Slope sections were modeled using the SLOPE/W 2004 software published by Geo-Slope International Ltd., and analyzed using the force-moment-equilibrium criteria of the Bishop Method.  Soil strength parameters were chosen based on the relative density or consistency of the soil derived from site-specific borehole information.  Where the density/consistency of the soil ranges, the lower limit parameters were selected for modeling.  The highest detected groundwater and cave-in levels from the boreholes were incorporated in the analysis as a phreatic surface, with an assumed profile to drain towards the slope.  Where applicable, surcharge loads of 5 kPa and 10 kPa were added 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 5 
to account for vehicular (driveway) and house loadings, respectively. 
 
The analyses yield the global factor of safety (FOS) for the existing slopes, which is then compared to the Ontario Ministry of Natural Resources (OMNR) guideline requirements for active land use (minimum FOS 1.5).  Where the existing slopes fail to satisfy the OMNR requirement, a geotechnically stable gradient ranging from 1V:2.0 to 2.6H is applied in the native soils, and a gradient of 1V:2.5 or 3.0H is used in the earth fill for establishing a stable slope.    In addition, a toe erosion setback will be required in the absence of an adequate floodplain (a minimum floodplain width of 15.0 m).  Where active erosion was observed along the tributary bank, an erosion allowance of 8.0 m is applied, considering that the lower stratigraphy of the slopes consists of mainly compact to dense and stiff to hard  clay, tills or granular strata.  Allowances are also considered where active erosion was not observed but the associated floodplain width was below the required minimum.  Selection of such allowance, as suggested in the OMNR guideline, is based on the bankfull width of the watercourse at the toe of the slope and the site-specific subsoil condition.  The toe erosion setback was generally omitted where functional shoreline protection schemes are already in place, effectively preventing toe erosion along the watercourse.  The Long-Term Stable Slope Line (LTSSL), incorporating the stable gradient and toe erosion setbacks, if any, is presented on the stable/remodeled slope Drawing Nos. 1 to 73.  As revealed, the LTSSL will cut into the majority of the existing residential house envelopes.  In order to reduce the hazards identified and to maintain the available space at the tableland for residential use, the slope should be stabilized and protected from further surface erosion and/or prevent future global failure.  Various slope stabilization schemes, such as reinforced earth and mechanically stabilized earth walls (MSE), gravity  retaining walls, soil nailing and Geoweb systems, are recommended based on 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 6 
site results.  Detail descriptions of the stabilization options are included in Appendix B.  
 
For surficial erosion control, the use of erosion control blankets and/or planting of deep-rooting vegetation systems should be installed/employed on the finished slope surface, with proper vegetation designed by a landscape architect.  The installation of the erosion control mats must follow the manufacturer’s specifications.  In case of any removal of vegetation during the course of construction, restoration with selective native plantings, including deep rooting systems which would penetrate the original buried topsoil, must be carried out after the development to ensure bank stability. The surrounding areas should be graded to divert surface runoff away from the slope as concentrated surface drainage from the sites must not be allowed to drain onto the bank.  Details of the site conditions and the stability analysis for each property are discussed in the following sections.
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 41 
 
 
       
21, 23 and 25 PEACHAM CRESCENT 
 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 42 
 
The 3 residential properties are located on the south side of Peacham Crescent, along the 
northern bank of the valley and trail system.  Tableland features include grass lawns, a shed at House No. 21, retaining walls and fence lines at the top of slope.  The houses are approximately 10 to 15 m from the existing top of bank.  
Subsurface Condition (Boreholes 28, 29, 27S to 29S)  
Beneath a layer of topsoil fill, 15± cm thick, and a layer of earth fill extending to depths of 0.8± m and 1.5± m, the site is underlain by a complex stratigraphy consisting of generally very stiff silty clay and clay till and dense sandy silt till, interstratified with layers of compact to dense sandy silt, compact to very dense silty fine sand and very dense fine sand.  The earth fill consists of mainly silty clay and sandy silt material, with some topsoil inclusions and roots.  Groundwater was detected in 1 of the 2 deep boreholes at a depth of 6.7 m (El. 148.3 m) upon completion of the field work.  When measured again one month later, the groundwater level had risen to a depth of 5.4 m (El. 149.6 m).  Sample examinations reveal that the sands found in the lower stratigraphy are generally wet and water-bearing.  
Slope Condition 
The slope height is approximately 8± m, with an overall slope gradient ranging from 
1V:1.19 to 1.27H±, and local gradients of 1V:0.58 to 3.46H±.  The creek, located approximately 5 m away from the existing toe of slope, is channeled and protected on both sides by gabion baskets.  The slope face is wooded, with mature trees and shrubs. Majority of the trees are standing in an upright position, with the exception of some leaning trees where erosion scarring has occurred.  Deep-seated failure was observed near House Nos. 23 and 25 at the crest of the slope.  Exposed tree roots were observed and surface sloughing is evident along steep sections.  The retaining structures and 
 Reference No. 1403-S070 (A) 43 
fences are failing, or have already failed. 
 
Slope Stability Analysis and Remediation  
Based on the soil densities revealed by the borehole information, the following soil 
strength parameters were selected for the slope stability analyses.    Soil Strength Parameters
