5.2.3 Mitigative Measures  
Digging will not be required in the area identified in Figure 18; however , as this area will be heavily used by 
delivery trucks,  a subsurface investigation was completed for this pipe. Daylighting was carried out on April 14, 
2022, including four  daylightin g holes to a maximum depth of 1.8 m. The daylighting revealed large amounts of 
debris, including asphalt, large rocks , and pieces of curb . The pipe was not exposed during daylighting  and is 
assumed to be  located below this layer. Based on the results, a ri sk mitigation report was issued recommending 
several mitigation measures while travelling over the pipe to prevent damage. These include:  
• not raising the grade by greater than 1 m or stockpiling overtop of the pipe,  
• not cutting the grade a height less than  1.3 m over the pipe, and  
• preventing risk to the water valve either by locating it using ground -penetrating radar, or by maintaining 
a 2m distance around the area of the valve.  

Humber Bay Park East Shoreline Maintenance Project: Phase II – Western Headland  
Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    21 
 This investigation was carried out to prepare for Phase I of the works. TRCA st aff will continue to follow these 
mitigation measures during Phase II  which will maintain the  same access route  into the site . 
6 SCOPE OF WORK  
The following scope of work will be completed as part of major maintenance for Phase I I to ensure long -term 
protection of the shoreline in the project area.  
 Construction Phasing  
The scope of work for Phase I I will include the items listed below  and will be completed in the following general 
sequence:  
1. Site setup including e stablish ment of  staging/stockpiling areas  at the western headland , remov al of 
required trees,  and install ation of  ESC measures, tree protection, and site perimeter control .  
2. Limited regrading of native fill material to accommodate repair works  and establishment  of 
construction road where necessary.  
3. Repair of the  Eastern Headland  Transition by establishing a backshore armourstone wall and 
headland to create a small habitat embayment. This will include:  
a. Excavation of the toe and backshore as n ecessary and stockpiling of reusable  material from 
the retaining wall area . 
b. Cons truct terminus of Phase I revetment component to tie into armourstone ret aining wall .  
c. Installation of geotextile base and 300 -600 mm rip rap in excavated area for stacked 
armourstone wall . 
d. Place ment of 3 -5 tonne armourstone in a stacked formation to create a wall along the back 
of the embayment . 
e. Filling of excavated area in front of the retaining wall with armourstone and existing 
material.  
f. Installation of 3 -5 tonne cap stone along the crest of t he revetment and 2 -4 tonne along the 
crest of the retaining wall in a special placement configuration .  
g. Installation of shoal using 600-800 mm subangular stone.  Due to constructability, t his 
component may be insta lled by barge during Ph ase III rather than d uring Phase II.  
h. Placement of habitat features within the embayment area.  
4. Repair of the western  headland  will occur in  10m increments  proceeding from west to east . This will  
include:  
a. Removal and stockpiling of crest stone  and backshore excavation  as necessary . 
b. Placement of  imported and stockpiled  armourstone (size range varies by station) in a 
random placement configuration along the slop e of the existing structure . Some 
repositioning of the existing stone may be necessary to ensure stability . 
c. Installation of a geotextile base and 300-600 mm  rip rap along crest . 
d. Installation of 3-5 tonne cap stone along crest  in a special placement configuration . 
e. Placement of habitat stone where appropriate . 
Humber Bay Park East Shoreline Maintenance Project: Phase II – Western Headland  
Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    22 
 5. Repair of the pond outlet area by creating an armourstone berm that allows for drainage of the 
ponds. This will include:  
a. Excavation of the existing bed to prepare for installation of the armourstone . 
b. Placement of the geotextile base and 300 -600 mm as core stone  as well as 3 -5 tonne 
armourstones to act as toe stones . 
c. Placement of  imported and stockpiled 2 -4 tonne  armourstone in a random placement 
configuration above the ri p rap base to create the berm . 
d. Placement of 3 -5 tonne armourstone  along the crest of the backshore and at the toe o f the 
structure on the pond and the la keward sides . 
6. Backshore regrading  and preliminary restoration (topsoil and seeding)  
7. Full s ite restoration, including compensation plantings and restoration of path features to return  the 
area to a safe and functional state , to be completed following the implementation of all three 
phases . Portions of the access route and staging will be maintained for subsequent phases . 
 Detailed Scope of Work  
The overall approach to the designs was to prioritize long -term resiliency while reducing the need for excavation 
and off -site disposal to limit disturbance and impacts of the construction activities  as well as addressing the 
leading erosion concerns of th e park, including low crest elevation and wave overtopping. The desig ns address 
these concerns by placing new material over the existing structures where toe and slope stability permits  
thereby minimizing excavation requirements. The designs  were developed  using a  100-year  design water level of 
76.2  m.a.s.l  and the structur es are designed to ensure the overtopping rate is below 10 litres/second.  
6.2.1 Western Armourstone Headland  
The treatment for most of the headland (stations 0+ 000 to 0+225) includes placement of new armourstone over 
the existing profile in order to elevate  the shore as shown in  the plan views in  Figure 19. The slope o f the  
revetment structure will consist of  randomly placed armourstone  or rip rap  of various size ranges built at a slope 
of 2h:1v . Some minor repositioning of the existing structure may be necessary to ensure stability.  The stone size 
ranges  vary by the level of protection required as determined by the condition of the structure and the results of 
the coastal analysis . Newly plac ed stone  will generally be either 400-800 mm rip rap, or 1-2, 2-4, or 3-5 tonne 
armour stone . 
The crest elevation will be built up to a range of 77.5 to 79.5 m.a.s.l. with a width that ranges from 2 -5 m wide. 
The existing armourstone s along the crest will be removed  and stockpiled and some minor excavation of the 
backshore will be required. All stockpiled and excavated material will be reused onsite. The crest will be 
constructed using a 300 -600 mm underlayer of rip rap overtop of a geotextile base  layer and capped w ith a 
single layer of 3 -5 tonne armourstone in a special placement configuration.  A portion of the r ip rap base layer 
will form a sp lash pad behin d the crest stone.  The backshore and the adjacent trail will be raised to an elevation 
ranging from 77 to 79 m.a.s.l. using Granular B and capped with compacted topsoil. The shoreward side o f the 
trail will have a slope of 1% and the land ward side of the trail will have a 5% slope for drainage. The cross  
sections are shown in Figure 20. 
Humber Bay Park East Shoreline Maintenance Project: Phase II – Western Headland  
Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    23

6.2.2 Pond Outlet  
The treatment for the Pond Outlet  (stations 0+275 to 0+325) focuses on reinstating the shoreline protection and 
formalizing a drainage route from the adjacent pond system through the shoreline structure. This will consist of 
an armourstone berm and plug of randomly placed 2  - 4 tonne armourstone over a base layer of 300 – 600 mm 
rip rap. The berm will be constructed to a minimum elevation of 76 m and a maximum elevation of 78 m ( Figure 
21). The higher elevation section  will create a pooling area for the pond  system while the low elevation area will 
allow the pool to drain into the lake . Existing drainage mechanisms from the actual pond sys tem will not be 
impacted as part of this work. In addition, the design includes a scattered stone element near the eastern 

Humber Bay Park East Shoreline Maintenance Project: Phase II – Western Headland  
Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    24 
 terminus to help retain beach material that will eventually be placed to the east of the structure as part of Phase 
III.  
Excavation will be required to install the structure , as shown in Figure 22. It is anticipated tha t some of this 
material can be reused for regrading the backshore, and any concrete material that is excavated that meets the 
rip rap size criteria can be reused in the base layer of the structure.

6.2.3 Eastern Headland T ransition  
The treatment for this section includes an armourstone node and retaining wall system to preserve and protect 
the existin g aquatic habitat feature that has formed over time  (Figure 23 and Figure 24). The design includes a 
shoal to help contain the nearby beach , which will be finalized in Phase III. The existing informa l trail  behind the 
structure will need to be rerouted to accommodate this design. Details of the trail design will be in cluded in the 
final restoration plan that will be circulated with Phase III.  
The retaining wall component will be constructed using 3 -5 tonne stacked armourstone  with 2 -4 tonne 
armourstone  along the crest . This will be constructed in front of and on top of  a base of 300 -600 mm rip rap . 
Additional randomly -placed armourstone  will be placed in front of the wall and buried with existing material  for 
toe protecti on. The shoal  is made of 600 -800 m m sub -angular stone  that extends into the lake. The purpose o f 
the shoal  is to help contain the beach materia l and protect the em bayment area from filling in with beach stone. 
The design may be adjusted when Phase III is finalized. Due to the  depth of  the shoal, construction may need  to 
be undertaken using a barge. If this is the case, the shoal will not be implemented until Phase III so it can be  
placed  by barge  along with the beach  material .

 6.3.1 Surcharged Revetment  
Habitat features were installed as part of Phase I , consist ing of surcharge d stone at the base of the revetment at 
several points along the deepest part of the structure.  A similar approach is planned for Phase II along the 
Western Armourstone Headland . The surcharged revetment will include  the placement of  stone material at the 
toe or lower slope of the structure , rang ing in size from 100 -600 mm  (Figure 25). Larger  material within  this 
range will be cast beyond lakeward  in order to hold smaller material in place  along  the lower slope of the 
revetment. The material will be placed in a random pattern in strategic locations across portions of the 
revetment length. Optimal placement will be confirmed onsite based on existing conditions, focusing on areas 
where existing off shore material does not exist , while maintaining navigation depth requirements. This 
methodology is meant to enhance pre -existing offshore habitat pockets that are believed to have developed as a 
result of material washout from the previous structure failu re. Exact locations of the features  will be determined 
based on site conditions . Due to strong wave conditions modeled in the project area, material may naturally 
shift and resettle over  time.  
 
Figure 25. An example of surcharge stone at the toe of a revetment to act as aquatic habitat. Source: TRCA 2019.  
6.3.2 Embayment  
The Eastern Headland Transition  was i dentified by TRCA ’s AMM staff as good -quality fish habitat. To preserve 
this habitat, the design for this area has been updated from a revetment to an embayment/headland structure, 
as described in Section 6.2.3 . This will preserve existing high quality fish habitat and refuge along the park 
shoreline . In addition to preserving this embayment, s everal features will be added to the area to enhance the 
existing fish habitat, including submerged randomly placed 300 -600 mm rip rap at the mouth of the embayment, 
surcharged sand along the base of the retaining wall, and a small number of submerged armourstone  placed 
sporadically within the embayment area ( Figure 26). All features will be constructed using existing materials on -
site.

Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    28 
  
Figure 26. Habitat features for the Eastern Headland Transition. Source: Shoreplan, 2023.

road onto an informal trail via the access point shown below in Figure 27. Trucks will drive southeast to the first 
staging and stockpiling area  on the west side of the site which was established during Phase I construction . For 
work happening at the Western Headland, trucks will travel along the trail to a proposed s taging area at the tip 
of the headland. For trucks working at the Pond Outlet, they will turn left south of the first staging area to access 

Humber Bay Park East Shoreline Maintenance Project: Phase II – Western Headland  
Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    29 
 the site. Trucks working at the Eastern Headland Tr ansition  will continue  east along the beach crossing the 
constructed berm with a culvert  at the Pond Outlet. The temporary culvert w as installed to allow for passage of 
trucks along the shoreline while still accommodating the drainage requirements for the ponds in the interior of 
the park.  The Eastern Headland  Transition will use the eastern staging area that was established during Phase I  
construction . During high wind and wave conditions , trucks will deposit materials at the western staging area.

 Required Tree Removals  
As part of the tree inventory , all trees above 10 cm diameter at breast height (DBH) as well as memorial or 
recently planted trees  were measured and tagged.  Any trees that require removal or will be potentially injured 
during the works were identified and are listed in Section 3.3 of the Arborist Report.  Tree removals will be kept 
to a minimum and be in accordance with TRCA policies.  Each phase will be permitted separately for Urban 
Forestry. The permit submission for Phas e II include s 30 trees, 62 whips, and 7 potential injuries  and is f urther 
discussed in Section 13.1 . Some trees alo ng the access route s and in work areas that were part of Phase I have 
already were permitted and removed as part of that phase and are not included in  the Phase II permit . 
 Hazardous /Stinging  Plants Screening  
No hazardous  or stinging  plants were  noted on site by TRCA Surveying staff or during tree inventories completed 
by Forestry Services . Site conditions may have changed since the screening was completed and Construction 
staff should undertake a site -specific workplace hazard assessment of hazardous plants.  

Humber Bay Park East Shoreline Maintenance Project: Phase II – Western Headland  
Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    30 
 9 EROSION A ND SEDIMENT CONTROL MEASURES  
Prior to the start of construction, staging and stockpiling areas  will be isolated with standard silt socks  to prevent 
the entry of deleterious substances into the watercourse , as shown previously Figure 27. All barriers will be 
inspected and maintained in proper working order throughout the duration of construction and will remain in 
place until the site is sufficiently stabilized.  
All waste mat erials will be removed from the work site to prevent them from entering the  lake. 
At the end of each working day exposed soils shall be stabilized with appropriate erosion control matting where 
appropriate. Construction should be phased in a manner that limits the size of disturbed areas and minimizes 
clearing/grading. In general, excav ation should be limited to an area that can be stabilized by the end of the day 
to reduce the risk of leaving soil exposed for any prolonged duration. All disturbed areas shall be stabilized as 
soon as possible following construction and restored as descri bed in Section 13. 
10 MEASURES TO PROTECT FISH AND FISH HABITAT  
The following measures will be used to protect any fish and their habitat : 
• Existing trail s, roads, and cut lines will be used wherever possible to avoid excess disturbance of riparian 
vegetation.  
• The removal of existing vegetation will be kept to an absolute minimum.  
• Staff will minimize the required works within the watercourse and along its b anks. Construction shall 
proceed in a continuous fashion to minimize the duration of work.  
• Aquatic monitoring will be undertake n to ensure in -water works do not impact spawning fish  where 
necessary.  
• As stone will be used during construction of the in-water structures , the following measures will be 
incorporated to protect fish habitat:  
o Appropriately sized, clean rock will be placed to stabilize the area of concern.  
o Rocks will not be obtained from belo w the ordinary high -water mark of any water body.  
o Rock that is acid generated will be avoided  as will rock that f ractures and breaks down quickly when 
exposed to the elements.  
o Machinery will be kept in clean condition and in good working order to prevent t he entry of any 
deleterious substances into the lake. Machinery shall be refueled no less than 30 metres from the lake.  
11 CONSTRUCTION BEST MANAGEMENT PRACTICES  
The proposed construction phasing sequence, as discussed in Section  6, recognizes site constraints, access 
routes, staging , storage requirements, and construction timing windows to facilitate the approved activities. The 
following best management practices (BMPs) will be employed during construction to ensure the ongoing 
protection of the environment and public safety:  
Humber Bay Park East Shoreline Maintenance Project: Phase II – Western Headland  
Project Brief  
 
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    31 
 • A spill  kit shall be kept on site at all times in the event of a spill resulting from machine breakdown or 
damage.  
• Tree protection barriers will be erected where necessary and will be void of any grade changes and storage 
of materials/equipment within the Tree Pr otection Zone (TPZ).  
• All disturbed areas are to be restored to existing conditions or better. Any disturbed areas will be vegetated 
by planting and seeding with native trees, shrubs , and grasses to prevent erosion. In the event that there is 
insufficient t ime remaining in the growing season, the site will be stabilized e.g., cover exposed areas with 
erosion control blankets to keep the soil in place and prevent erosion , and the plantings will be completed 
during the next appropriate planting window. In acco rdance with this, effective erosion and sediment 
control measures will be maintained until site is re -vegetated.  
• Machinery and vehicles will be kept clean of debris and seeds in order to prevent the spread of invasive 
species.  
12 CONSTRUCTION TIMING  
Construction of Phase I  began in November of 2021 beginning  at the eastern limits of the armourstone headland  
and proceed ing westward s. Phase I is anticipated to take 18 months in total, with completion by spring of  2023. 
Following completion of Phase I, construction will immediately proceed to Phase II in late spring/early summer 
of 2023, and is  anticipated to take approximately 14 months . Phase II will begin with the Eastern Headland 
Transition . Following this, the Eastern Headland will be preliminarily restored and work will begin at the western 
limit of the Western Headland and proceed toward the Pond Outlet.  
Due to the duration of the work, permissions have been received from DFO to work through the restricted 
activity timing windows if necessary. Efforts will be ta ken to prioritize in -water works  outside of these windows, 
but due to the scale of the project, it is likely that in-water works w ithin the fall and spring windows are likely to 
occur. Monitoring data shows that there are three specie s of fall spawning fish and four species of spring 
spawning fish. The three fall -spawning fish  – Atlantic Salmon, Chinook Salmon , and Brown Trout  – use river 
systems as spawning grounds  therefore  construction activities would not interfere  with these species.  The f our 
species of fish sampled during monitoring tend to spawn in lakes. Of these four species, Rainbow Smelt and 
Alewives  are not native to the area, Logperch spawn in area s absent of swif t currents  and may avoid the waves 
of the open coast , and the Emerald Shiner typically spawn in June when waters are warmer. Based on 
monitoring records, T RCA staff recommend weekly sampling be done  from  early  June to mid-July 2023 and if 
any spawning fish  are detected, then in -water works will cease . 
Although constru ction for Phase II is  not scheduled to be gin until late spring/ early summer, required tree 
removals will be undertaken before April 15, 202 3. This timin g will avoid the bird breeding season  and will 
mitigate the risk of  potentially destroying nests and eggs of sen sitive bird sp ecies . Crews  currently mob ilized  for 
Phase I will undertake these removals once permits are finalized.

Phase I to allow for public access  to a portion of the park . Until this final  restor ation plan is developed, 
preliminary planting plans have been  draft ed for Phases I  and II. These plans represent a c ommitment to plant a 
certain number of tr ees duri ng final restoration and will be comb ined, updated and finalized into the full 
planting plan  for the site . 
The Phase I preliminary plan inv olves t he on-site planting of 2 80 trees  whose approximate loc ations are  shown 
in Figure 28. Plantings will c onform to Section 7 of the Phase I Arborist  Report.  Open  areas that were d istur bed 
during construction , such as the staging and stockpiling area , will be seed ed using TRCA ’s Ontario  Resilient Area 
Meadow Mix (TRCA -SD-4).

 Post Construction Monitoring  
The site will be inspected during the first year after major storm events and on an annual basis thereafter to

1 INTRODUCTION  
Humber Bay Park is a waterfront park  that is located at the mouth of Mimico Creek  on the north shore of Lake 
Ontario. The park consists of two peninsulas  (Humber Bay Park E ast and Humber Bay Park West ) that extend  out 
into Lake Ontario.  Park construction began in the 1970s  as a lake -filling operation which reached its current form 
in the 1990s . The parklands are armoured with a series of headlands and beaches  to protect the shoreline from 
erosion. The park is a large urban green space, featuring wetlands, forests, and meado ws, as well as a number of 
cultural and natural heritage features  including park trails, a marina, the Air India Memorial, and the Humber Bay 
Butterfly Habitat Project. The park is heavily used by the local community and this usage is expected to increase 
as the neighbourhood evolves into a denser, high -rise residential community.  
Erosion control structures , including headlands and beaches,  were built  in the early 1980s  in order to protect the 
shoreline . Toronto and Region Conservation Authority’s (TRCA) Er osion Risk Management Program (ERMP)  has 
monitored these structures  on an annual basis  since 2006.  Both t he western armourstone headland (WF 11.10) 
and the  cobble/gravel beach (WF11.11) are currently  classified as in overall “fair” condition, but with a structural 
stability rating of “failing” due to several deficiencies . The eastern armourstone headland  (WF11.12) is classified 
as in overall “poor” condition with a structural stability rating of “failing”  due to its deficiencies .  
In the fall of 2016, Riggs Engineering Limited undertook a comprehensive assessment of the 73 TRCA -owned 
shoreline erosion control structures between Marie Curtis Park in the west and the western extent of Ontario 
Place in th e east. Based on the ranking system accounting for structure condition, adjacent land use function, 
environmental factors, and others, Humber Bay Park  (East and West ) ranked fifth  overall in priority. Since the  
comprehensive assessment took place, the deterioration of these structures has been exacerbated by  the 2017 
and 2019  high lake level events as well as the  April 14 -15, 2018  wind storm. Major maintenance is required to 
return these structures to a state of good repair and provide long -term protection to the Humber Bay Park East 
shoreline.  
  PROJECT NAME  Humber Bay Park East Major Maintenance Project  
REGION  Etobicoke, City of Toronto  
TRCA DIVISION  Restoration and Infrastructure (Engineering Projects)

Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    1 2 SITE DESCRIPTION  
 Location  
The site is located in Humber Bay Park East , along the north shore of  Lake Ontario in  Etobicoke, City of Toronto . 
The closest major intersection is  Lake Shore Boulevard West and Park Lawn Road  with t he park accessible via 
Marine Pa rade  Drive . The general location of the site and erosion control structures are shown below in Figure 1.  
 
Figure 1. Map of Hu mber Bay Park East and location of erosion control structures. Source: TRCA, 2019.  
 Land Usage  
The area adjacent to the structures is parkland  and includes formal and informal trails  that run parallel to the 
shoreline . The park features a system of streams and ponds, one of which drains at the eastern limit of the western 
headland (WF11.10)  as shown in Figure 2.

 Typical Slope/Channel Dimensions  
The shoreline erosion control structures  extend approximately 2 m above the waterline. The crest of the 
structure s are  around 77 metres above- sea-level (m.a.s.l.)  with most of the park at an elevation of about 78 m.a.s.l.  
The typical near shore depth is approx imately 72 -73 m.a.s.l. A contour map pf the park is shown in Figure 13.

4 PERMITS  
The permits and approvals process will commence during the detailed design phase. All applicable permits and 
approvals will be obtained prior to implementation.  
5 CONCEPT DESIGNS 
The overall approach to the concept designs aims to prioritize  long- term resiliency  while  reducing the need for  
excavation and off -site disposal in order to limit disturbance and impacts of the  construction activities  while 
Humber Bay Park East Major Maintenance Project –  Concept  Brief  
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    12 addressing the leading erosion concerns of the park , including low crest elevation and wave overtopping.  The 
proposed concepts have been designed to  address these concerns by plac ing new material over the existing 
structure s where toe and slope stability permits , thereby minimizing excavation requirements . Two  sections have 
been recommend ed to undergo a full reconstruction  where damage to the shoreline  is extensive and the existing 
material is not stable enough to act as core material.   The concepts were developed using a design water level of 
75.8 m.a.s.l. and were designed to ensure that the overtopping rate is below 10 litres/second.  
 WF11.10 – Western Headland  
The treatment outlined by the concept designs for  the western  headland  includes  the placement of fill over the 
existing profile . The  crest elevations at the western extent will be raised to 77 m.a.s.l. using 300-600mm rip rap  
and will transition to a 3-5 tonne  armourstone treatment with a crest elevation of 78.5 ma.s.l. at the southern 
extent of the structure.  The armourstone treatment will transition to an  elevation of 77.8 m.a.s.l.  at the eastern 
extent of the headland . Please see the plan view and cross -sections in Figure 14 and Figure 15. Armourstone sizes 
vary based on the requirements of the treatment; the more exposed areas on the southern tip of the structure 
require 3 -5 tonne armourstone, while more sheltered areas near t he eastern limit require 2 -3 tonne armourstone . 
 
Figure 14. Planview of c oncept designs for structure WF11.10.  Red lines denote cross -sections shown  in later figures . Source: 
Shoreplan, 2020.

Humber Bay Park East Major Maintenance Project –  Concept  Brief  
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    14 At its eastern limit, the headland  transitions into beach  WF11.11. At this transition point, the concept design 
includes  the creation of a berm , consisting of  2-3 tonne armourstone , to create a formal outlet area for the pond s 
(Figure 16 and Figure 17). The elevation of the treatment will be 78.5 m .a.s.l. (Figure 17). The pond will drain into 
the lake through a  plug of loosely placed armourstone that will have crevices to allow the  water to filter through.  
The design  was developed with consideration of  maximum outflow  conditions, which were calculated to be  1000  
g/minute.  This treatment will also facilitate the creation of a backwater  or wetland area between the pond and 
the outlet since  water will naturally pool behind the berm . The design also includes  the presence of scattered 
stone in front of the berm to help hold  in the to e of the adjacent beach ( Figure 18).

Humber Bay Park East Major Maintenance Project –  Concept  Brief  
Toronto and Region Conservation Authority    |    17 In general, s maller cobble sizes will offer a more user- friendly beach environment for park users than larger stone , 
but more material will be required to sufficiently protect the shoreline. Treatments using smaller cobble  will 
therefore have higher costs and a greater in -water footprint as well as greater potential  for maintenance  needs 
following large storm events . Conversely, l arger cobble sizes will allow for a  smaller in-water  footprint , but will  
create a rougher surface and a less user -friendly  beach environment.  The overall cost for a larger cobble size will 
be lower with  less frequent maintenance needs . The selection of the preferred cobble size will be made  through 
discussion s with TRCA, City of Toronto , and Shoreplan Engineering Limited  and will consid er overall cost, in -water 
footprint, maintenance requirements, user experience , and structure  aesthetics . 
 
The eastern limit of the beach is heavily damaged, as shown above in Figure 8, and its proposed treatment requires 
the extension of the eastern headland into the beach area (sections 0+550 to 0+600 on the drawings). This 
treatment is described in the following section w ith the treatment of the eastern headland (WF11.12).   
 WF11.12 – Eastern Headland  
The concepts  for the eastern headland  involve  place ment of fill over  most of  the existing profile  supplemented 
with a n extension of the structure toward the beach  for the heavily damaged area located between sections 0+550 
to 0+600 on the drawings  (highlighted in yellow on Figure 21). The proposed treatment for the re construct ed 
section (station 0+575) is shown in blue on the cross sections and includes the placement  of rip rap as a core 
material capped with 2 -3 tonne arm ourstone , as presented  in Figure 22. The reconstruction will require 
excavation of the existing profile and placement of fill beneath or behind the stru cture. This treatment provides 
alternative options for crest elevation, crest width and slope positioning : the black option presents the highest 
and narrowest possible crest (78.5 m.a.s.l. and 3.0 m wide) while the green option presents the lowest and wide st 
possible crest (77.5 m.a.s.l. and 7.0 m wide) . The structure can be designed to these specifications or to any 
elevation in between. In general, if the crest is built to a lower elevation it will need to be built wider.   
The proposed treatment for the  rest of the headland  (sections 0+625 to 1+225)  includes placement of  3-5 tonne 
armourstone fill over the existing profile  as shown in Figure 22, cross -sections 0+850 and 1+150 . Similar to the 
treatment described above, alternative options for crest elevations and widths  are provided  for various  sections, 
shown in green and black on the cross -sections . In general, a higher crest  will require less excavation and a lesser 
impact on the backshore areas  but may obscure lake sight lines. This would be mitigated in the design; fill would 
be used to raise the elevation of the backshore areas  to ensure that there is a maximum differentia l no greater 
than 1m between the backshore and crest elevations . Wider crests would require move clearing and vegetation 
removal and  will encroach further into parkland and  park paths , however, sightlines would be maintained and it 
is less likely that rais ing backshore elevation would be necessary.  
Further assessment of the backshore conditions, including locations of existing trails and presence of vegetation, 
will be conducted for each area. This will help determine the options that will have the least im pact for each 
section.  Additional discussions between TRCA,  City of Toronto and Shoreplan Engineering Limited  will be required 
in order to select the preferred option s. In addition to the recommendations of the backshore assessment, c ost, 
maintenance requirements and aesthetics will be key considerations throughout the selection process.
